Concluded briefly as needed. [2] He said: 'or remains silent...' Know that nukul may be literal, like saying 'I will not swear', or constructive [by remaining silent]; its ruling is the same as the former when it is known that there is no disability of muteness or deafness; that is the correct view. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The author explicitly mentioned silence because there is disagreement – some scholars say it is not ruling of nukul, but the correct view is what has passed. [3] He said: 'valid' meaning that judgment. Al-Shafi'i said: The judge does not pass judgment by nukul; rather, he returns the oath to the plaintiff; if he refuses, the dispute ceases; if he swears, he passes judgment by it, based on what was narrated from Ali that he made the plaintiff swear after the defendant's nukul. [PAGE_105] Book of Lawsuit / Its Definition and Rulings 105. And because the oath was initially required of the denier because the apparent evidence supports him; when he refuses, the apparent evidence becomes in favor of the plaintiff, so he swears. And because nukul could be due to confusion of the situation – he does not know whether he is truthful in his denial (so he would swear) or lying (so he refrains) – or due to scrupulousness about a false oath, or due to being above a truthful oath, as Uthman did when he refused the oath and said: 'I fear that a decree may correspond [to a false oath],' so it is said – regarding Uthman – 'he swore falsely'; thus it is not a proof due to possibility, so judgment is not made by it, and the plaintiff's oath is evidence of his being truthful in his claim, just as the defendant's oath was, so it reverts to the plaintiff's oath. Our proof is the consensus of the Companions, and it is narrated from Ali that he agreed with their consensus. It is narrated from Shurayh that the defendant sought to return the oath to the plaintiff, and he said: 'You have no way to do that,' and he judged by nukul in the presence of Ali, who said to him: 'Qanoon' – meaning in Greek: 'You are correct.' And it is narrated from Umar that a woman claimed before him that her husband said to her: 'Your camel's rope is on your shoulder,' so Umar made the husband swear: 'By Allah, did you intend divorce?' He refused, so he passed judgment of separation. Similarly from Ibn Abbas, and it is the school of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. And because nukul indicates that the defendant is [ready to] concede if nukul is a substitute, as is the view of the Imam [Abu Hanifa], or affirms [the claim] if nukul is an admission, as is their view [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]; if not, he would have proceeded to the oath to fulfill the obligation and repel harm from himself. So this aspect outweighs others like being above [swearing], scrupulousness, and confusion, because the apparent is that he performs the obligation, so he does not refrain from a truthful oath, and the apparent from a Muslim is that he does not lie, so his nukul is not scrupulousness about a false oath considering his apparent state. And if it were due to confusion of the situation, he would have sought respite until the matter was clarified. So it is determined that it is due to [ready to] concede, and there is no basis for returning the oath to the plaintiff, because of what is narrated: 'The oath is upon the denier.' Thus they said.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is an expansion on the ruling of nukul (refusal to take an oath) in litigation. The author first states the ruling: if the defendant refuses the oath once (explicitly or by silence without a disability), the judge may pass judgment by nukul, and the oath is offered three times. The author clarifies that nukul can be literal (saying 'I will not swear') or constructive (silence when no disability like muteness). The correct view is that both are treated the same.

The author then presents an intra-Hanafi sub-issue: according to Abu Yusuf, the judge administers an oath without the plaintiff's request in four specific cases: (1) buyer swearing in return for defect, (2) preemptor swearing, (3) woman swearing to get maintenance from absent husband, (4) rightful claimant swearing. Then a consensus is mentioned: anyone claiming a debt against a deceased must swear a detailed oath without request from the executor/heir.

The main discussion is the inter-madhhab dispute. Al-Shafi'i held that the judge should not judge by nukul; rather, he should return the oath to the plaintiff. If the plaintiff swears, judgment is for him; if he also refuses, the dispute ends. The Shafi'i proof is a narration from Ali that he made the plaintiff swear after the defendant's nukul, and rational arguments: the oath was initially on the denier because apparent evidence supports him; after nukul, the apparent evidence shifts to the plaintiff; nukul could be due to confusion, scrupulousness, or being above swearing, so it cannot be definitive.

The Hanafi response (Lana) cites consensus of Companions (ijma' al-sahaba) and specific narrations: Shurayh judged by nukul in Ali's presence, and Ali approved in Greek saying 'Qanoon' (you are correct). Also Umar judged separation when a husband refused to swear. The Hanafi rationale: nukul indicates that the defendant is either ready to concede (if nukul is a substitute for the oath according to Abu Hanifa) or affirming the claim (if nukul is an admission according to the Sahibayn). If not, he would have sworn to fulfill obligation and avoid harm. Possibilities like scrupulousness or being above swearing are outweighed because a Muslim normally performs obligations and does not lie. If confused, he would ask for time. Thus, nukul is a ground for judgment, and the oath is not returned to the plaintiff because the established principle is 'the oath is upon the denier.'

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal to take the oath after being required to; occurs literally (saying 'I will not swear') or constructively (silence without disability).
اليمين (al-yamin): The oath administered to the defendant (or plaintiff) in court to establish a claim or defense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of the defendant's nukul (refusal to swear)?
A) The judge returns the oath to the plaintiff.
B) The judge immediately rules against the defendant.
C) The judge dismisses the case.
D) The judge offers the oath three times and then rules against the defendant if he persists.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the defendant's nukul (refusal of the oath) after three offers is a sufficient basis for the judge to rule against him, without returning the oath to the plaintiff.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Ruling by Defendant's Refusal to Swear (Nukul) – Proofs and Hanafi Position
Hanafi proofs that nukul leads to judgment for plaintiff

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on nukul, identify the key proofs (including ijma), and distinguish the two Hanafi views on its legal nature.

Core Idea
The defendant's refusal to swear (nukul) leads to judgment against him—this is proved by the Consensus of the Companions and rational inference.

This passage examines one of the most important procedural rulings in Hanafi fiqh: the effect of a defendant's refusal to take an oath (nukul). While the Shafi'i school returns the oath to the plaintiff, the Hanafi school holds that nukul itself is sufficient for judgment. The author presents both rational and transmitted proofs, including a key Consensus of the Companions. We will work through the proofs to understand how the Hanafi position is established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its legal effect
What is the ruling when the defendant refuses to swear? The text states that judgment is given in favor of the plaintiff. Understand the practical outcome.
The ruling applies in qada (judicial proceedings).
2
Examine the rational arguments (istidlal bi al-mashhud)
The text first argues that the oath was initially on the defendant because apparent evidence supports him. When he refuses, the apparent shifts to the plaintiff. It then considers possible reasons for refusal (confusion, piety, pride) and argues that the most likely reasons are inability to swear truthfully or obstinacy, implying the claim is valid.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
3
Locate the transmitted proof (ijma)
The text states 'We have: the consensus of the Companions.' It then cites specific actions of Ali, Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Identify each narration and how it supports judgment by nukul.
Ijma is a primary source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the nature of nukul
Imam Abu Hanifa considers nukul as a substitute (badal) for the oath, implying the defendant acknowledges the claim indirectly. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it an admission (iqrar) directly. Understand the difference in theoretical characterization.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the outcome.
5
Confirm that both views lead to the same outcome
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the same: judgment against the defendant. The text does not prefer one over the other; both are valid positions. Recognize that the ruling is established regardless of the interpretation.
The mufta bihi is that nukul leads to judgment.

Source Text

ولأنَّ اليمين إنما وجبت في الابتداء على المنكر ؛ لكونِ الظَّاهرِ يشهد له ، فإذا نكل هـ كان الظاهر شاهداً للمدعي، فيحلف ؛ ولأنَّ النكول يحتمل أن يكون لأجل اشتباء الحال عليه بأن لا يدري صادق في إنكاره فيحلف، أو كاذب فيمتنع، أو لأجل التورع عن اليمين الكاذبة. أو لأجل الترفع عن الصادقة، كما فعل عثمان ، فإنه نكـل عـن اليمين ، وقال : أخاف أن يوافقه قضاء، فيقال - أي عثمان - : حلف كاذباً فلا يكون حجة مع الاحتمال، فلا يقضي به ويمينُ المدَّعي دليل ظهور كونه محقاً في دعواه ، كما كانت يمين المدعى عليه، فيرجع إلى يمين المدعي. ولنا : إجماعُ الصَّحابة ، وروي عن علي الله أيضاً أنه وافق إجماعهم، فإنّه روي عن شريح له : إنَّ المنكر طلب منه ردُّ اليمين عن المدعي، فقال : ليس لك إليه سبيل، وقضى بالنكول بين يدي علي الله ، فقال لـه علـي : قانون، ومعناها بالرومية : أصبت. وروي عن عمر له أنّ امرأة ادعت عنده على زوجها أنه قال لها : حبلك على غاربك، فحلف عمرُ الله الزوج : بالله أردت طلاقاً ، فنكل، فقضى عليه بالفرقة،
وكذا روي عن ابن عباس الله ، وهو مذهب أبي موسى الأشعري له. ولأن النُّكول دل على كون المدعى عليه باذلاً إن كان النكول بدلاً، كما هو قولُ الإمام، أو مقراً إن كان النكولُ إقراراً ، كما هو قولهما ، إذ لولا ذلك لأقدم على اليمين أداء للواجب، ودفعاً للضرر عن نفسه، فترجحت هذه الجهة على غيرها من الترفع والتورع والاشتباه ؛ لأنَّ الظاهر أنه يأتي بالواجب، فلا يرتفع عن الصادقة. والظاهر من حال المسلم أنه لا يكذب، فلا يكون نكولُه تورعاً عن الكاذبة ظاهراً باعتبار حاله ولو كان لاشتباءِ الحالِ لاسْتَمْهَلَ حتى ينكشف له الحال، فتعين أن يكونَ لأجل البذل، ولا وجه لرد اليمين على المدَّعي ؛ لما روي من أن اليمين على المنكر. كذا قالوا.
The Book of Claims / Its Definition and Rulings. And because the oath was obligated initially upon the defendant because the apparent (evidence) supports him; so when he refrains (nukul), the apparent becomes evidence for the plaintiff, so he swears. And because nukul could be due to confusion about his situation: he does not know whether he is truthful in his denial so he hesitates, or he is lying so he refrains, or due to piety to avoid a false oath, or due to pride from a truthful oath, as did Uthman, for he refrained from the oath and said: 'I fear that a decree may correspond (with my oath), and it will be said – meaning Uthman – swore falsely.' So it is not a proof with possibility, so judgment is not given by it. And the plaintiff's oath is evidence of his being truthful in his claim, just as the defendant's oath was, so it returns to the plaintiff's oath. We have: the consensus of the Companions, and it is reported from Ali that he agreed with their consensus. Indeed, it is reported from Shurayh that the defendant asked him to return the oath to the plaintiff, and he said: 'You have no way to that,' and he gave judgment by nukul in the presence of Ali, who said to him: 'Qanun,' meaning in Roman: 'You are correct.' And it is reported from Umar that a woman claimed before him against her husband that he said to her: 'Your burden is on your hump,' so Umar made the husband swear: 'By Allah, I intended divorce,' and he refrained, so he gave judgment of separation. Similarly reported from Ibn Abbas, and it is the madhhab of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. And because nukul indicates that the defendant is paying (badal) if nukul is a substitute, as is the view of the Imam, or confessing if nukul is an admission, as is their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because otherwise he would have proceeded to the oath to fulfill the obligation and repel harm from himself. So this aspect (of badal/admission) outweighs other aspects of pride, piety, and confusion, because the apparent is that he performs the obligation, so he does not refrain from a truthful oath. And the apparent state of a Muslim is that he does not lie, so his nukul is not out of piety from a false oath apparently considering his state. And if it were due to confusion, he would have requested a delay until the situation became clear for him. So it is determined that it is for the sake of payment (badal). And there is no basis for returning the oath to the plaintiff due to the reported tradition: 'The oath is upon the defendant.' Thus they said.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi proofs for the ruling that when a defendant (منكر) refuses to take an oath (نكول), judgment is given in favor of the plaintiff. The author first gives rational arguments: the defendant's refusal shifts the apparent evidence to the plaintiff. He then addresses possible motivations for refusal (confusion, piety, pride, etc.) and argues that the most likely motives are either inability to swear truthfully (implying admission) or obstinacy (implying liability). He cites the consensus of the Companions (إجماع الصحابة) as the primary evidence, followed by specific reports from Ali, Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The passage also notes the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa considers nukul as a substitute (بدل) for the oath, whereas Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it an admission (إقرار). In either case, the result is judgment against the defendant. The final point: the oath is not returned to the plaintiff because the established rule is 'the oath is upon the defendant' (اليمين على المنكر).

Key Terms
النُّكول (al-nukūl): The defendant's refusal to take the oath after being asked by the judge.
اليمين (al-yamīn): The oath taken by a litigant to support his claim or denial.
المنكر (al-munkir): The defendant who denies the claim.
المدعي (al-mudda'ī): The plaintiff who brings the claim.
إجماع الصحابة (ijmā' al-ṣaḥābah): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet Muhammad, cited as a proof for ruling by nukul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary transmitted proof for ruling by nukul?
A) The hadith 'The oath is upon the defendant'
B) The Consensus of the Companions (ijma as-sahabah)
C) The practice of the caliph Umar
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules by nukul based on the Consensus of the Companions and rational inference, with two accepted interpretations of its legal nature (badal or iqrar) that both lead to judgment against the defendant.

Repetition of Warning and Immediacy of Judgment after Nukul
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repetition of warning and immediacy of judgment after nukul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the obligatory and recommended views on repeating the oath offer to the defendant, and state the Hanafi position on immediate judgment after nukul.

Core Idea
A judge may rule after one warning; repeating three times is recommended, and immediate judgment is not required except in three specific cases.

The judge's procedure after the defendant refuses the oath (nukul) involves two debated points: how many times the judge must warn the defendant before ruling, and whether the ruling must be immediate. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya refines the Hanafi position, showing that the relied-upon view is that one warning suffices and delay is permissible except in three exceptional cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two intra-Hanafi disputes
The passage discusses (1) whether repeating the oath offer is obligatory or recommended, and (2) whether the judge must rule immediately after nukul or can delay.
Both involve the procedure after nukul.
2
Extract the views attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn)
They held that repetition of the warning is obligatory (hatm), so a ruling after one warning would not be executable (la yanfudh).
This is the strict view.
3
Contrast with the 'correct' (sahih) view
The correct view is that judgment after one warning is executable (yanfudh) and repeating three times is recommended (mustahab), analogous to the three-day respite for apostates.
The warning itself is necessary to inform the defendant, as rule by nukul is not universally known.
4
Analyze the dispute on immediacy
Some shaykhs required immediate judgment; al-Khassaf and the three imams allowed a delay of up to three days if the plaintiff requests it or there is hope of reconciliation among relatives.
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar states that judgment is presumed immediate except in three cases.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position: judgment is valid after one warning; three warnings are recommended. Immediate judgment is preferable but not mandatory, with three exceptions: doubt in evidence, plaintiff's request for delay, and hope of reconciliation among relatives.
Al-Hidayah affirms this as the correct view.

Source Text

ثم القضاء أحوط
ثم القضاء أحوط )
قوله : أحوط ؛ أي على وجه الندب، قالوا: ينبغي للقاضي أن يقول : إنّي أعرض عليك اليمين، فإن حلفت وإلا قضيتُ عليك بما ادعاه ، وهذا الإنذار لإعلامِهِ بالحكم إذ الحكم بالنكول موضعَ الخفاء ؛ لكونه مجتهداً فيه، فإنَّ عند الشافعي له لا يحكم بالتكول، بل يردُّ اليمين على المدعي ، فإذا كَرَّرَ عليه الإنذار والعرض ولم يحلف حكِمَ عليه، إذا عَلِمَ أنه لآفة به من طرش وخرس ونحوهما.
قال في «التبيين» : وعن أبي يوسف ومحمد إنَّ التكرار حَتْم حتى لو قضى القاضي بالنكول مرَّة لا ينفذ ، والصحيح أنه ينفذ ، والعرض ثلاثاً مستحب، وهو نظير إمهال المرتد ثلاثة أيام فإنه مستحب ؛ فكذا هذا مبالغة في الإنذار، ولا بُدَّ أن يكون التكولُ في مجلس القاضي ؛ لأنَّ المعتبر يمينُ قاطع للخصومة، ولا معتبر باليمين عند غيره في حق الخصومة، فلا يعتبر. انتهى. وهل يشترط القضاء على فورِ النُّكول؟ فيه اختلاف ؛ قال في «المجتبى»: يشترطُ أن يكون القضاء على فور النكول عن بعض المشايخ، وقال الخصاف : لا يشترط ، حتى لو استمهله بعد العرض يوماً أو يومين أو ثلاثة فلا بأس به، وهو قول الأئمة الثلاثة. انتهى.
وقال في «المنح» : لم أر فيه ترجيحاً. انتهى. وقال في «الهداية» : هذا التكرار ذكره الخصَّافُ الله له الزيادة الاحتياط والمبالغة في إبلاء العذر، فأما المذهب أنه لو قضى بالنكول بعد العرض مرَّةً جاز لما قدمنا ، هو الصحيح، والأول أولى. انتهى.
وقال في «الدر المختار» : قدَّمنا أنه يفترض القضاء فورا إلا في ثلاث. انتهى. وهي أن يرتابَ القاضي في طريق القضاء كالبينة، وأن يستمهل الخصم : أي المدعي وأن يكون لـرجاء الصلح بين الأقارب، وظاهره أنه لا خلاف. هكذا في «حاشية الطحطاوي)، وغيرها.
Cream of the Finality for the Support of the Care. Then the judgment is more cautious. Then the judgment is more cautious. His saying: 'more cautious' means on the basis of recommendation. They said: It is appropriate for the judge to say: 'I present the oath to you; if you swear, otherwise I will give judgment against you for what he claimed.' This warning is to inform him of the ruling because the ruling by nukul is a place of concealment, as it is a matter of ijtihad. For according to al-Shafi'i, he does not rule by nukul, but returns the oath to the plaintiff. So if he repeats the warning and presentation and he does not swear, he rules against him, when he knows that he has an impediment such as deafness, muteness, or the like. It is stated in al-Tabyin: From Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that repetition is obligatory, such that if the judge ruled by nukul once, it would not be executable. But the correct view is that it is executable, and presenting three times is recommended. This is analogous to giving a renegade a respite of three days, for it is recommended. So this is exaggeration in warning. And it is necessary that the nukul be in the judge's court, because the oath that cuts off litigation is considered, and the oath elsewhere is not considered in terms of litigation. End. And is immediate judgment after nukul required? There is disagreement. It is stated in al-Mujtaba: Immediate judgment after nukul is required from some shaykhs. Al-Khassaf said: It is not required, even if he asks for a delay after the presentation of a day, two days, or three, there is no harm, and it is the saying of the three imams. End. And it is stated in al-Munah: I have not seen a preponderance on it. End. And al-Hidayah states: This repetition was mentioned by al-Khassaf for extra caution and exaggeration in excusing. As for the madhhab, if he judges by nukul after one presentation, it is permissible based on what we have presented; that is the correct view, and the first is better. End. And al-Durr al-Mukhtar states: We have presented that it is assumed to judge immediately except in three cases. End. They are: that the judge doubts the means of judgment like evidence, that the opponent (i.e., the plaintiff) asks for a delay, and that there is hope of reconciliation between relatives. Its apparent meaning is that there is no disagreement. Thus in Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and others.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hāshiya) that refines the discussion on the judge's procedure after nukul. It begins by explaining that the phrase 'the judgment is more cautious' (ثم القضاء أحوط) means it is recommended (ندب), not obligatory. The judge should warn the defendant by saying 'I present the oath; if you swear, otherwise I will judge against you.' This warning is necessary because the ruling by nukul is not universally known; it is a matter of ijtihad, especially since the Shafi'i school does not rule by nukul. The passage then discusses two key controversies: (1) Whether the judge must repeat the offer of oath. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad reportedly considered repetition obligatory, but the correct view is that it is recommended (mustahab), analogous to the three-day respite for apostates. (2) Whether judgment must be immediately after nukul. Al-Khassaf and the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that it is not required; a delay of up to three days is permissible. However, some shaykhs required immediacy. Al-Munah found no preponderance, but al-Hidayah affirms that judgment after one warning is valid and the first position (repetition) is better. Finally, al-Durr al-Mukhtar states that judgment is presumed immediate except in three cases: doubt in the evidence, a request by the plaintiff for delay, or hope of reconciliation among relatives.

Key Terms
العرض (al-'arḍ): The judge's presentation of the oath to the defendant, typically accompanied by a warning of judgment upon refusal.
الإنذار (al-inḏār): The warning given by the judge to the defendant about the consequences of refusing the oath.
التكرار (al-takrār): Repeating the presentation of the oath to the defendant, typically recommended up to three times.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the requirement to give judgment immediately after nukul without delay.
الاستمهال (al-istimhāl): Asking for a delay; the plaintiff may request a delay for certain reasons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is obligatory (hatm) for the ruling to be valid
B) It is recommended (mustahab) but not required
C) It is forbidden because it delays justice
D) It is required only for the plaintiff

Key Takeaway
The judge may rule after one warning, though repeating three times is recommended; immediate judgment is not required except in three specific cases.

Judge’s Recommendation to Repeat Oath Offer
Commentary on judge repeating oath thrice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating the oath offer, distinguish the mufta bihi from the minority view, and apply the conditions for immediate judgment after nukul.

Core Idea
Repeating the oath thrice is mustahabb, not wajib; judgment after one refusal is valid.

In this passage, the commentator explains the phrase 'ثم القضاء أحوط' (then judgment is more precautionary) from the base text. The key issue is whether a judge must repeat the oath offer three times before ruling against a defendant who refuses to swear. The passage unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute and clarifies the relied-upon position, while also addressing whether judgment must be immediate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and commentary orientation
The base phrase 'ثم القضاء أحوط' is being explained. The commentator clarifies that 'أحوط' here means recommended (nadb), not obligatory. This sets the tone for the entire discussion.
The warning to the defendant is to inform him of the consequence, because the ruling on nukul is a matter of ijtihad.
2
Distinguish recommended vs. obligatory repetition
Two views are presented: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say repetition is obligatory (hatm) so judgment after one offer is invalid. The correct view (sahih) is that judgment after one offer is valid, and repeating thrice is mustahabb.
The analogy is drawn to the apostate's three-day respite, which is also mustahabb.
3
Analyze the analogy to the apostate’s respite
Just as giving the apostate three days is recommended but not required, repeating the oath offer three times is recommended to give the defendant every chance. The hadith 'al-bayyina ala al-mudda'i...' does not mandate repetition.
This analogy (qiyas) supports the mutamad view.
4
Understand the immediacy of judgment after nukul
There is disagreement on whether judgment must be immediate (fawr). Some say yes, but al-Khassaf and the three imams allow a delay of up to three days. Al-Durr al-Mukhtar states that judgment is required immediately except in three cases: doubt about the evidence, plaintiff requests delay, or hope of reconciliation.
These exceptions are agreed upon and prevent injustice.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that judgment after one offer is valid; repetition is mustahabb. Judgment should be immediate unless one of the three exceptions applies.
Al-Hidaya confirms this as the correct view.

Then judgment is more precautionary. His saying: 'more precautionary' means as recommended. They said: It is befitting for the judge to say: I offer you the oath; if you swear, otherwise I will give judgment against you based on what is claimed. This warning is to inform him of the ruling because judgment based on nukul (refusal to swear) is a point of hiddenness, as it is a matter of ijtihad. For according to al-Shafi'i, he does not judge based on nukul, but rather returns the oath to the plaintiff. Al-Khassaf said: It is not required; even if he asks for a delay of one, two, or three days after the offer, there is no harm. This is the saying of the three imams. End. Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya on the base text phrase 'ثم القضاء أحوط' (Then judgment is more precautionary). The commentator explains that 'أحوط' here means on the basis of recommendation (nadb), not obligation. He details the procedure: the judge should offer the oath to the defendant, warn him that refusal will lead to judgment. This warning is necessary because the ruling based on nukul is not obvious, especially since Imam al-Shafi'i does not accept nukul as grounds for judgment but returns the oath to the plaintiff. The commentator then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, repeating the offer (tasbia') is obligatory (hatm) such that if the judge judges after one offer, the judgment is not enforceable. However, the correct view (sahih) is that it is enforceable, and repeating thrice is merely recommended (mustahabb). This is likened to giving an apostate three days’ respite. The passage then discusses whether judgment must be immediate after nukul. Some scholars require immediacy, while al-Khassaf and the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) allow a delay of up to three days. No preponderance is seen in al-Minh. Al-Hidaya confirms that judgment after one offer is valid (sahih) but the first view (repetition) is better. Finally, al-Durr al-Mukhtar states that judgment is required immediately except in three cases: when the judge is uncertain about the method (e.g., reliability of evidence), when the plaintiff asks for a delay, and when there is hope of reconciliation between relatives. The commentator notes that these exceptions are agreed upon.

Key Terms
نكول (nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath after being offered by the judge.
يمين (yameen): The oath administered to the defendant in court.
فور (fawr): Immediacy; judgment must be pronounced immediately after nukul unless exceptions apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Repeating thrice is recommended (mustahabb), but judgment after one offer is valid.
C) Repeating thrice is prohibited (haram) because it delays justice.
D) The judge must never repeat; one offer is the only valid option.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the judge may rule after one offer of the oath; repeating thrice is recommended, not required, and judgment should be immediate unless one of three exceptions applies.

Oath Not Returned and Not Administered in Specific Matters
Commentary on two rules: no return of oath on nukul, and no oath in specific matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on nukul (defendant's refusal to swear) and the nine exceptional cases where the defendant is not sworn, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The oath is never returned to the plaintiff, and in nine specific matters the defendant is not sworn at all.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies two critical procedural principles: first, that upon the defendant's refusal to swear (nukul), the oath is not transferred to the plaintiff—rather, judgment is given against the defendant; second, there are nine exceptional matters where the defendant is not sworn at all, even if he denies the claim. We will examine the primary proof from hadith, the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two rulings
The passage presents two separate rules: (a) the oath is not returned to the plaintiff on nukul; (b) in nine specific matters (nikah, ruj'a, fay' in ila', istilad, riqq, nasab, wala') the defendant is not sworn at all. Identify the scope of each rule.
These are procedural rules of qada'.
2
Identify the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith 'al-bayyina 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara' (The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies). Explain how this hadith prohibits returning the oath to the plaintiff.
The Hanafi school considers this hadith as the foundational evidence.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute (Shafi'i)
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that upon nukul, the oath is returned to the plaintiff. The commentator labels this a bid'ah and attributes it to Mu'awiya. Compare the two positions and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The dispute is over the correct procedure after nukul.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute (nine matters)
Abu Hanifa says the defendant is not sworn in these nine matters; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say he is sworn. Understand the basis for Abu Hanifa's view and note that his position is the mufta bihi.
The list of nine matters is cut off in the text; only seven are explicitly mentioned.

واستقل بها بعدما صالح معه سيدنا الحسن بن سيدنا علي ، ومات في رجب سنة سنين الله ، وكان صحابياً جليلاً، وفقيهاً نبيلاً، دعا له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حيث قال : «اللهمَّ عَلم معاوية الحساب والكتاب ، وقهِ العذاب (۳) ، وأحوال المفصلة مزبورة في «الإصابة» وغيرها من التواريخ المبسوطة.
(۳) قوله : ولا يحلف المنكر عند الإمام خلافاً لصاحبيه في تسعة أمور : ا نكاح : قال القُهستاني (4) : أي نفس النكاح أو الرضا به، أو الأمر به، فلو ادعى أحد من الزوجين بلا بينة نكاحاً على الآخر، وهو منكره لم يحلف عنده ، بل .
And the oath is not returned to the plaintiff even if his opponent refuses (to swear). There is disagreement with al-Shafi'i, for according to him when the opponent refuses (nukul), the oath is returned to the plaintiff. This is an innovation (bid'a), and the first to rule by it was Mu'awiya, and it contradicts the well-known hadith. According to us: And he is not sworn in (matters of) marriage, revocation (رجعة), return (فيء) in Ila', istilad (acknowledgment of paternity of a slave concubine's child), slavery, lineage, and patronage (wala'). Know that in these cases, according to Abu Hanifa he is not sworn, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is sworn. And its explanation: [1] His saying: 'And it is not returned' etc., because he said: 'The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies,' and it is not permissible to nullify the division of the Shari'ah. [2] His saying: 'Mu'awiya' – his kunya is Abu Abd al-Rahman, and he is the son of Abu Sufyan Sakhr ibn Harb ibn Umayya al-Umawi. He embraced Islam on the day of the Conquest (of Mecca), and it is said before the Conquest. He accompanied the Prophet (peace be upon him) and was the scribe of revelation. He was the first to govern Syria under Umar and Uthman, and he became independent after Hasan ibn Ali made peace with him. He died in Rajab in the year 60 (AH). He was a noble Companion and a distinguished jurist. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed for him saying: 'O Allah, teach Mu'awiya calculation and writing, and protect him from the punishment.' His detailed biography is recorded in al-Isabah and other comprehensive histories. [3] His saying: 'The defendant is not sworn according to the Imam, contrary to his two companions, in nine matters: (1) Marriage: al-Quhistani said: meaning the marriage itself, or consent to it, or the command for it. So if one of the spouses claims without evidence a marriage against the other, and the other denies it, he is not sworn according to him (Abu Hanifa), but...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two rulings from the base text about oaths in court proceedings. First, 'ولا يرد اليمين على مدع وإن نكل خصمه' – the oath is not returned to the plaintiff even if the defendant refuses to swear. The commentator notes the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that when the defendant refuses, the oath is transferred to the plaintiff. The Hanafi position is based on the well-known hadith 'البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر' (The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies). The commentator adds that returning the oath to the plaintiff is a bid'ah (innovation) first practiced by Mu'awiya (RA). A brief biography of Mu'awiya is provided, highlighting his status as a Companion, scribe of revelation, and the subject of a prophetic prayer. The second ruling is 'ولا يحلف في نكاح ورجعة وفيء في إيلاء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء' – the oath is not administered (to the defendant) in matters of marriage, revocation (رجعة), return in Ila', acknowledgment of paternity of a slave concubine's child (istilad), slavery, lineage, and patronage (wala'). Commentator explains that, according to Abu Hanifa, the defendant is not sworn in these nine matters (the text mentions seven here, but the full list is nine). However, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the defendant is sworn. The passage then begins to detail the first case (marriage) but cuts off.

Key Terms
نكول (nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath; leads to judgment against him in Hanafi law.
بدعة (bid'ah): Innovation in religion; here the commentator labels the Shafi'i practice of returning the oath as a bid'ah because it contradicts the established hadith.
إيلاء (ila'): A vow by the husband to abstain from marital relations for a period of four months or more.
استيلاد (istilad): A master's acknowledgment of paternity of his slave concubine's child, making her an umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens when the defendant refuses to take the oath (nukul)?
A) The oath is returned to the plaintiff.
B) The judge gives judgment against the defendant.
C) The case is dismissed.
D) The defendant is imprisoned until he swears.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'al-bayyina 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara' is the foundation for not returning the oath; in nine specific matters, according to Abu Hanifa, the defendant is not sworn.

Oath Not Returned to Plaintiff Even if Defendant Refuses
Explaining the ruling and rebutting Shafi'i on oath return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that the oath is not returned to the plaintiff, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith and the bid'ah critique.

Core Idea
The oath is a fixed right of the defendant; it never shifts to the plaintiff, even if the defendant refuses.

This passage addresses a key procedural dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. When a defendant refuses to swear the oath, should the judge offer the oath to the plaintiff? The commentator explains the Hanafi ruling, supported by the well-known hadith, and then rebuts the Shafi'i view, labeling it as an innovation (bid'ah). Understanding this disagreement is crucial for correctly applying Islamic court procedure.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the oath is never returned to the plaintiff, even if the defendant refuses to swear.
The text explicitly says 'ولا يرد اليمين على مدع'.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Read the hadith cited: 'البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر' and understand how it fixes the division of proof and oath.
The hadith is the primary proof; the division is considered absolute and cannot be altered.
3
Present the opposing view
Describe Imam al-Shafi'i's position that the oath is returned to the plaintiff if the defendant refuses.
This is the view the commentator criticizes.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand why the Hanafis label the returned oath as a bid'ah, tracing it to Mu'awiyah, and how it contradicts the hadith.
The commentator uses strong language: 'هذا بدعة' – this is an innovation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the dispute: under Hanafi law, refusal leads to judgment against the defendant; under Shafi'i, the plaintiff could swear and win.
This difference affects court procedure significantly.

Source Text

ولا يرد اليمين على مدع وإن نكل خصمه

[٢] قوله : معاوية ه ، كنيته أبو عبد الرحمن ، وهو ابن أبي سفيان صخر بن حرب بن أمية الأموي، أسلم يوم الفتح ، وقيل : قبل الفتح، وصحب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وكان كاتب الوحي ، أولي إمارة الشام عن حضرة سيدنا عمر وسيدنا عثمان .

The Book of Claims: Its Definition and Rulings. And the oath is not returned to the plaintiff, even if his opponent refuses (to swear). (1) And the oath is not returned to the plaintiff even if his opponent refuses; in this there is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i, for according to him, when the opponent refuses, the oath is returned to the plaintiff. This is an innovation, and the first to rule by it was Mu'awiyah, and it contradicts the well-known hadith. According to us, the defendant is not sworn. [1] His saying: 'And the oath is not returned ...' because he said: 'The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies,' and it is not permissible to nullify the division of the Law. [2] His saying: 'Mu'awiyah' - his kunyah is Abu 'Abd al-Rahman, and he is the son of Abu Sufyan Sakhr ibn Harb ibn Umayyah al-Umawi. He accepted Islam on the day of the Conquest, and it is said before the Conquest. He accompanied the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and he was a scribe of the revelation. He was appointed governor of Syria by our master 'Umar and our master 'Uthman. He became independent after our master al-Hasan ibn our master 'Ali made peace with him. Detailed accounts are recorded in 'al-Isabah' and other extensive histories.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the rule of returning the oath. The matn states that the oath is not returned to the plaintiff even if the defendant refuses to swear. The commentator explains that Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, holding that if the defendant refuses, the oath is returned to the plaintiff. The Hanafi position is that this is an innovation (bid'ah) first practiced by Mu'awiyah, and it contradicts the well-known hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies.' The commentator then provides a biographical note on Mu'awiyah, confirming his status as a Companion and scribe of revelation, and mentions the prophetic prayer for him. The key point is that the division of proof and oath established by the Law cannot be altered; the defendant must swear or be held liable, but the oath never shifts to the plaintiff.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): The oath sworn by the defendant in a legal claim to deny the plaintiff's allegation.
النكول (al-nukul): The defendant's refusal to swear the oath after being required to do so.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religious matters; here used to criticize the practice of returning the oath as contradicting established Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the defendant in a claim refuses to swear the oath?
A) The oath is returned to the plaintiff, who may swear and win the case.
B) The defendant is compelled to swear or judgment is given against him.
C) The case is dismissed.
D) The judge takes an oath on behalf of the defendant.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the oath is an exclusive obligation of the defendant; if he refuses, judgment goes against him, and the oath is never transferred to the plaintiff.

Nine Cases Where Abu Hanifa Does Not Administer the Oath
Listing nine cases with intra-madhab dispute and financial exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nine cases where Imam Abu Hanifa does not administer an oath to the defendant and explain the dispute with the Sahibayn, including the exception for financial claims.

Core Idea
In personal status matters, Abu Hanifa waives the oath; Sahibayn analogize to financial claims and require it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a distinct intra-Hanafi disagreement: in nine specific cases involving marriage, revocable return, slavery, lineage, and wala, Imam Abu Hanifa refrains from administering an oath to the defendant, while his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, insist on it. The disagreement turns on whether these matters are purely personal or have financial implications. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to distinguish when a defendant's oath is required in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
Abu Hanifa's default ruling is that the defendant is not sworn in nine specific cases. List them: marriage (nikah), revocable return (raj'ah), return in ila (fay'), istilad, slavery (riqq), lineage (nasab), wala of emancipation, wala of clientage, and one more (possibly the tenth? The text says nine, but lists several; we'll treat them as nine categories).
The exact enumeration varies slightly, but the core principle is consistent.
2
Contrast with the Sahibayn's view
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the defendant must be sworn in all these cases, just as in any ordinary claim.
They analogize these personal matters to financial disputes where oath is standard.
3
Analyze the underlying principle
Abu Hanifa sees these as personal status matters where the claim itself carries weight or where an oath would lead to false swearing or hardship. The Sahibayn see the oath as a universal tool to protect defendants.
This is a qiyas vs. istihsan distinction: Sahibayn use qiyas on general claims, Abu Hanifa uses istihsan based on the nature of the case.
4
Determine the practical difference
In pure personal claims (no financial element), Abu Hanifa's view prevails: no oath. But if the claim includes a financial right (e.g., dower, maintenance), all agree the defendant is sworn.
This consensus exception is crucial for application.
5
Apply the nuance to a scenario
Given a dispute, first identify the core claim. If it is purely personal and listed among the nine, no oath under Abu Hanifa. If financial rights are attached, the oath is mandatory by consensus.
Always check for financial elements before ruling on the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يحلف في نكاح ورجعة وفيء في إيلاء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء
اعلم أنَّ في هذه الصُّورِ لا يستحلف عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما : يستحلف، وصورتها :
[٣] قوله : ولا يحلف المنكر عند الإمام خلافاً لصاحبيه في تسعة أمور : ا نكاح : قال القُهستاني : أي نفس النكاح أو الرضا به، أو الأمر به، فلو ادعى أحد من الزوجين بلا بينة نكاحاً على الآخر، وهو منكره لم يحلف عنده ، بل ادعى الرَّجلُ النكاح، وأنكرت المرأة أو بالعكس، أو ادعى الرَّجلُ بعد الطلاق وانقضاء العدَّةَ الرَّجعة في العدة، وأنكرت المرأة أو بالعكس، أو ادَّعى الرَّجلُ بعد انقضاءِ مُدَّةِ الإيلاء الفيء في المدَّة، وأنكرت المرأة أو بالعكس، وادعى الرَّجلُ على مجهول النَّسب أنَّه عبده أو ابنه ، وأنكر المجهول أو بالعكس. واختصما في ولاء العتاق، أو ولاء الموالاة على هذا الوجه، أو ادَّعت الأمة على مولاها أنَّها ولدت منه ولداً ، أو ادعاه وقد مات الولد، ولا يجري في هذه المسألة العكس؛ لأنَّ المولى إذا ادعى ذلك تصير أم ولد بإقراره لا اعتبار لإنكار الأمة.
يُعَلِّقُ حتى وجد البينة، ولها دفعُهُ بتحليف أنها إن كانت امرأتك فهي طالق ، ويحلف عندهما، فعند أبي يوسف له : بالله که تو یرازن نکرده ، وعند محمد ه : بالله که وي زن تونیست در بن حال، وهو أحوط ، كما في «القاعدي». انتهى. وذكر البرْجَنْدِي نقلاً عن «الظهيرية»: اختلف بعض المشايخ في دعوى المرأة النكاح، وإنكار الزوج أن يحلف بالله ما هي زوجة لي، فإن كانت هي زوجة لي فهي طالق بائن، وإنّما يحلف بالطلاق ؛ لأنه يجوز أن يكون كاذباً في الحلف بالله تعالى، ولا يقع الطلاق بذلك، فتبقى معطلة إن لم يقل ما ذكر. انتهى. وقال الطحطاوي في حاشية على الدر المختار) : ولا تحليف في نكاح مجرد عن المال عند الإمام له بأن ادعى رجل على امرأة أو هي عليه نكاحاً، والآخر ينكر، أما إذا ادعتِ المرأةُ تزوجها على كذا ، وادَّعتِ النفقة ، وأنكر الزوج يستحلف اتفاقاً. انتهى. وقال العيني في «الرمز (۲) : وكان ينبغي هاهنا قيد، وهو أن يقال في مجرَّدِ نكاح : يعني إذا لم يكن المقصود هو المال، وأما إذا كان القصد هو المال، كما إذا ادعت امرأةٌ على رجل أنه تزوجها بألف وطلقها قبل الدخول بها، ولها عليه نصف المهر، فإنّه يستحلف بالإجماع، فإن نكل قضى عليه بنصف المهر. انتهى.
٢ . ورجعة ؛ بأن يدعي أحدُ الزَّوجين بعد انقضاء العدَّةِ على الآخرِ أنه راجعها في العدة، والآخر ينكرها ، فإن ادَّعى الرجعة في العدَّة يثبت بقوله في الحال كما صرحوا به.
And he is not sworn in marriage, revocable return, return in ila, istilad, slavery, lineage, and wala. Know that in these cases, the defendant is not sworn according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (disciples) he is sworn. Their details: [3] His saying: The defendant is not sworn according to the Imam, contrary to his two companions, in nine matters: 1. Marriage: al-Quhustani said: i.e., the marriage itself, or consent to it, or commanding it. So if one of the spouses claims, without evidence, a marriage against the other, and the other denies it, he (the defendant) is not sworn according to him (Abu Hanifa). Rather, if the man claims marriage and the woman denies, or vice versa; or the man after divorce and expiry of the waiting period claims revocable return during the waiting period, and the woman denies, or vice versa; or the man after the expiry of the period of ila claims return during the period, and the woman denies, or vice versa; or a man claims against a person of unknown lineage that he is his slave or his son, and that person denies, or vice versa; or they dispute over wala of emancipation or wala of clientage in this manner; or a slave woman claims against her master that she gave birth to a child from him, or he claims that after the child has died, and the opposite does not apply in this case because if the master claims that, she becomes an umm walad by his acknowledgment, and the woman's denial is not considered. He (the defendant) is not sworn until evidence is found, and she (the plaintiff) can repel him by making him swear: 'If she is your wife, then she is divorced.' And according to the two, he swears. According to Abu Yusuf, the oath is: 'By Allah, you have not married?' and according to Muhammad: 'By Allah, she is not your wife in this situation,' and this is more precautionary, as in al-Qa'idi. End. And al-Barjandi narrated from al-Zahiriyyah: Some mashayikh differed in the case of a woman claiming marriage and the husband denying, that he swears by Allah: 'She is not my wife; if she is my wife, she is divorced irrevocably.' He only swears with divorce because he might be lying in swearing by Allah, and divorce does not occur by that, so she remains suspended if he does not say what was mentioned. End. And al-Tahtawi said in his hashia on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: There is no swearing in a marriage free from wealth according to the Imam, as when a man claims against a woman or she against him a marriage, and the other denies. But if the woman claims that he married her for such-and-such and claims maintenance, and the husband denies, he is sworn by consensus. End. And al-'Ayni said in al-Ramz: There should be a restriction here, that it should be said: in a mere marriage, meaning when the objective is not wealth. But if the objective is wealth, such as if a woman claims against a man that he married her for one thousand and divorced her before consummation, and she has half the dower against him, then he is sworn by consensus, and if he refuses, judgment is given for half the dower. End. 2. Revocable return: such as when one of the spouses after expiry of the waiting period claims against the other that he returned to her during the waiting period, and the other denies it. If he claims return during the waiting period, it is established by his statement immediately as they have explicitly stated.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute detailing nine cases where Imam Abu Hanifa does not administer the oath to the defendant, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do administer it. The cases are: (1) marriage - if one spouse claims marriage without evidence; (2) revocable return (رجعة) after divorce; (3) return in ila (فيء) during the waiting period; (4) istilad (claim of slave woman that her master fathered her child); (5-9) slavery, lineage, wala of emancipation, wala of clientage, etc. In these, Abu Hanifa does not require an oath because they are not purely financial matters; instead, the defendant is left to produce evidence. The two disciples analogize these cases to general claims and require the oath. The commentator then discusses nuances, especially regarding marriage when financial elements are involved: if there is a claim for dower or maintenance, the oath is administered by consensus. Practical examples are given, including the wording of the oath according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The passage emphasizes that the ruling changes when money is the objective, in which case all agree on swearing the defendant. Finally, the case of revocable return is clarified: the claim can establish the return immediately if made during the waiting period.

Key Terms
الرجعة (al-raj'ah): The revocable return of a wife during the waiting period after a revocable divorce, without a new contract.
الفيء (al-fay'): The return to marital relations by a husband who has taken an oath of ila (abstinence), which ends the ila period.
الاستيلاد (al-istilad): The claim that a slave woman has given birth to a child from her master, making her an umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A woman claims that the man married her for a dower of 500 dirhams.
B) A man claims that he returned to his wife during the waiting period, and the wife denies.
C) A man claims that the defendant borrowed 100 dirhams from him.
D) A seller claims that the buyer owes the price for goods sold.

Key Takeaway
In nine specific non-financial personal status matters, Imam Abu Hanifa does not require the defendant's oath, whereas the Sahibayn require it; however, if financial rights are involved, all agree on the oath.

Oath in Pure Status Claims: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Lists six types of legal claims and explains when the defendant is not required to take an oath according to Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on requiring an oath in pure status claims, explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify when the presence of a financial right changes the ruling.

Core Idea
In pure status claims without property, Abu Hanifa says no oath; Sahibayn require an oath—a key procedural difference.

This passage from the chapter on judicial claims (da'wa) lists six types of personal status disputes where no financial right is immediately claimed. The central issue is whether the defendant must be made to swear an oath when the claim is about marriage, divorce return (raj'ah), return in ila' (fay'), lineage, or slavery. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no oath is required, while his two disciples differ. The passage also clarifies that if a financial right is attached (like dower or maintenance), all agree on the oath. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying Hanafi procedure in family law cases.

Guided Path
1
List the six cases
Identify each of the six types of claims mentioned: marriage, raj'ah, fay', istilad (claim of child), slavery, and lineage.
These are all personal status claims without an immediate property element.
2
Understand the base ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, in these claims when no property is involved, the defendant is not required to swear an oath (la tahlif).
This is the default position of the Imam.
3
Note the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that an oath is required; they also specify the wording of the oath.
Muhammad's wording is considered ahwat (more cautious).
4
Recognize the exception for property
When a property right (e.g., dower, maintenance, inheritance) is attached, all authorities agree the defendant must swear.
This consensus (ittifaq) is highlighted by al-Ayni and al-Tahtawi.

ادعى الرَّجلُ النكاح، وأنكرت المرأة أو بالعكس، أو ادعى الرَّجلُ بعد الطلاق وانقضاء العدَّةَ الرَّجعة في العدة، وأنكرت المرأة أو بالعكس، أو ادَّعى الرَّجلُ بعد انقضاءِ مُدَّةِ الإيلاء الفيء في المدَّة، وأنكرت المرأة أو بالعكس، وادعى الرَّجلُ على مجهول النَّسب أنَّه عبده أو ابنه ، وأنكر المجهول أو بالعكس. واختصما في ولاء العتاق، أو ولاء الموالاة على هذا الوجه، أو ادَّعت الأمة على مولاها أنَّها ولدت منه ولداً ، أو ادعاه وقد مات الولد، ولا يجري في هذه المسألة العكس؛ لأنَّ المولى إذا ادعى ذلك تصير أم ولد بإقراره لا اعتبار لإنكار الأمة. يُعَلِّقُ حتى وجد البينة، ولها دفعُهُ بتحليف أنها إن كانت امرأتك فهي طالق ، ويحلف عندهما، فعند أبي يوسف له : بالله که تو یرازن نکرده ، وعند محمد ه : بالله که وي زن تونیست در بن حال، وهو أحوط ، كما في «القاعدي». انتهى. وذكر البرْجَنْدِي نقلاً عن «الظهيرية»: اختلف بعض المشايخ في دعوى المرأة النكاح، وإنكار الزوج أن يحلف بالله ما هي زوجة لي، فإن كانت هي زوجة لي فهي طالق بائن، وإنّما يحلف بالطلاق ؛ لأنه يجوز أن يكون كاذباً في الحلف بالله تعالى، ولا يقع الطلاق بذلك، فتبقى معطلة إن لم يقل ما ذكر. انتهى. وقال الطحطاوي في حاشية على الدر المختار) : ولا تحليف في نكاح مجرد عن المال عند الإمام له بأن ادعى رجل على امرأة أو هي عليه نكاحاً، والآخر ينكر، أما إذا ادعتِ المرأةُ تزوجها على كذا ، وادَّعتِ النفقة ، وأنكر الزوج يستحلف اتفاقاً. انتهى. وقال العيني في «الرمز (۲) : وكان ينبغي هاهنا قيد، وهو أن يقال في مجرَّدِ نكاح : يعني إذا لم يكن المقصود هو المال، وأما إذا كان القصد هو المال، كما إذا ادعت امرأةٌ على رجل أنه تزوجها بألف وطلقها قبل الدخول بها، ولها عليه نصف المهر، فإنّه يستحلف بالإجماع، فإن نكل قضى عليه بنصف المهر. انتهى. ٢ . ورجعة ؛ بأن يدعي أحدُ الزَّوجين بعد انقضاء العدَّةِ على الآخرِ أنه راجعها في العدة، والآخر ينكرها ، فإن ادَّعى الرجعة في العدَّة يثبت بقوله في الحال كما صرحوا به. ٣ . وفيء في إيلاء ؛ أي رجوع في مدة الإيلاء، بأن يدعي أحد على الآخر بعد مدة الإيلاء أنه فاءَ ورجع إليها في مدة الإيلاء، والآخر منكر، فإن اختلفا قبل المدة يثبتُ الفيء بقوله. كذا في «جامع الرموز»، وغيره. ٤. واستيلاد ؛ أي طلب ولد بأن يدَّعي أحدٌ من الأمة والمولى، أو الزوجة والزوج أنها ولدت منه ولداً حياً، أو ميتاً. كما في «قاضي خان»، لكن في المشاهير أن دعوى الزوج والمولى لم يتصوّر ؛ لأنَّ النسب يثبت بإقراره، ولا عبرة لإنكارها بعده، ويمكنُ أن يقال : إنه بحسب الظاهرِ لم يدَّعِ النَّسب ، كما دل عـلـيـه تــصـويرهم، كما في القهستاني)، فتدبر. وقال البرْجَندِي : ويمكن تصوير العكس، بأن حبلت الأمة من المولى وبعدما قربت الولادة أعتقها قبل وضع الحمل، وقبلت الولد وادَّعى المولى دية الولد عليها ، ولا بُدَّ في هذه الدعوى أولاً من ثبوت الولد، فأنكرت الأمة ذلك. انتهى. ٥ و٦ . ورق ونسب : بأن ادَّعى على مجهول أنه قنهُ أو ابنه : وبالعكس بأن ادّعى مجهول الحال على رجل أنه مولاه، وأنكر المولى، أو ادَّعى مجهول الحال عليه أنه أبوه ، وهذا في دعوى نسب مجرد عن المال. أما إذا ادعى مالاً بدعوى النَّسب بأن ادَّعى رجل على رجل أنه أخوه ، وقد مات الأب وترك مالاً في يد هذا، وطلب الميراث، أو ادَّعى على رجل أنه أخوه لأبيه ، وطلب من القاضي أن يفرض له النفقة، وأنكر المدعى عليه ذلك، فالقاضي يحلفه اتفاقاً ، صرح به العلامة الحموي وغيره. وقال الإثقاني: يثبت الاستحلافُ عند أبي يوسف ومحمد له في النسب المجرَّدِ بدون دعوى حق آخر، ولكن يشترط أن يثبت النسب بإقرار المقرّ : أي يكون النسب بحيث يثبت بالإقرار، أما إذا كان بحيث لا يثبت النسب بإقرار المقر، فلا يجري الاستحلافُ في النسب المجرد.
The man claims marriage, and the woman denies, or vice versa; or the man claims after divorce and expiry of the 'iddah that he returned (raj'ah) during the 'iddah, and the woman denies, or vice versa; or the man claims after the expiry of the period of ila' that he returned (fay') during the period, and the woman denies, or vice versa; and the man claims against a person of unknown lineage that he is his slave or his son, and the unknown denies, or vice versa; and they dispute over the wala' of manumission or the wala' of patronage in this manner; or a slave woman claims against her master that she gave birth to a child from him, or he claims it and the child has died, and the reverse is not applicable in this issue because if the master claims that, she becomes an umm walad by his admission, and the denial of the slave woman is not considered. He is suspended until he brings evidence, and she may repel him by demanding an oath: 'If she is your wife, she is divorced,' and he swears according to them. According to Abu Yusuf, he says: 'By Allah, you have not been married (??),' and according to Muhammad: 'By Allah, you are not my wife in this state,' and this is more cautious, as in al-Qa'idi. End. And al-Barjandi mentioned quoting from al-Zahiriyyah: 'Some mashayikh differed regarding the woman's claim of marriage and the husband's denial—he should swear: "By Allah, she is not my wife; if she is my wife, she is divorced thrice." And he only swears by divorce because he may be lying in swearing by Allah the Exalted, and divorce does not occur by that, so she remains suspended if he does not say what was mentioned.' End. And al-Tahtawi said in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'There is no oath in a marriage free from wealth according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], as when a man claims marriage against a woman or she against him, and the other denies. But if the woman claims that he married her for such-and-such and claims maintenance, and the husband denies, he is made to swear by agreement.' End. And al-Ayni said in al-Ramz: 'A restriction should be stated here: it should be said "in absolute marriage" meaning when the intent is not wealth. As for when the intent is wealth, such as when a woman claims that a man married her for one thousand and divorced her before consummation, and she has half the dower, then he is made to swear by consensus; if he refuses, he is ordered to pay half the dower.' End. 2. And [claim of] Raj'ah: that one of the spouses after the expiry of the 'iddah claims against the other that he had taken her back (rāja'a) during the 'iddah, and the other denies it. If he claims raj'ah during the 'iddah, it is established by his statement immediately, as they clarified. 3. And [claim of] Fay' in Ila': meaning return during the period of ila', that one claims against the other after the period of ila' that he returned (fā'a) to her during the period, and the other denies. If they differ before the period, the fay' is established by his statement. So in Jami' al-Rumuz and others. 4. And Istilād: meaning claiming a child, that one of the slave woman and master, or the wife and husband, claims that she gave birth to a live or dead child from him. As in Qadhi Khan. But in the mashahir, the claim of the husband and master is not conceivable because lineage is established by his admission, and her denial is disregarded thereafter. It may be said that in appearance he does not claim lineage, as indicated by their descriptions, as in al-Qahistani, so ponder. And al-Barjandī said: 'The reverse can be conceived: that the slave woman became pregnant from the master, and when delivery approached he freed her before the birth, and she accepted the child and the master claimed the child's blood money against her. This claim first requires establishing the child, so the slave woman denies that.' End. 5 and 6. [Claim of] Slavery and Lineage: that one claims against a person of unknown status that he is his slave or his son; and vice versa: that a person of unknown status claims against a man that he is his master, and the master denies; or a person of unknown status claims against him that he is his father. And this is in a claim of lineage free from wealth. As for when he claims wealth through the claim of lineage, such as a man claiming that another man is his brother, and the father has died leaving wealth in his hand, and he demands inheritance; or he claims that he is his paternal brother and asks the judge to impose maintenance; and the defendant denies; then the judge makes him swear by agreement, as declared by al-Hamawi and others. And al-Ithqani said: 'Oath-taking is established according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in purely lineage claims without a claim of another right, but with the condition that lineage can be established by the admission of the admitter: meaning that lineage is such that it can be established by admission. As for when it is such that lineage cannot be established by admission, then oath-taking does not apply in pure lineage claims.'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage from the book of claims (kitab al-da'wa) discusses a set of six types of legal claims where the dispute is purely about a personal status (marriage, return, lineage, slavery, etc.) without any immediate financial right attached. The central ruling presented is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, in such 'pure' claims, the defendant is not required to take an oath (لا تحليف). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ and hold that an oath is required. The passage then elaborates on the form of the oath and cites various authorities. The first and most detailed case is the claim of marriage (nikah). The text clarifies that if the claim involves a financial right (like dower or maintenance), then the defendant is made to swear by consensus. The remaining cases (رجعة, فيء, استيلاد, رق, نسب) are each briefly defined and the rule is applied: they are established by the claimant's statement if he swears, but the defendant's oath is not required. Special attention is given to the case of lineage (نسب) where the condition for oath is that the lineage must be such that it could be established by admission. The passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on a procedural point, and the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is not explicitly stated, but the text notes that Muhammad's formulation is 'more cautious' (أحوط).

Key Terms
استحلاف (istihlāf): The act of demanding or administering an oath from a party to a legal dispute to ascertain the truth or establish a claim.
رجعة (raj'ah): The return of a husband to his divorced wife during her 'iddah (waiting period) by which the marriage is revived without a new contract.
فيء (fay'): The return of a husband to his wife within the period of ila' (vow of abstinence), thereby breaking the vow and avoiding automatic divorce after the expiry of four months.
إيلاء (īlā'): A husband's vow to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for a period of four months or more, which can lead to divorce if he does not return within that time.
استيلاد (istīlād): The claim of a master or a husband that a female slave or wife gave birth to his child, thereby establishing the child's lineage and potentially the mother's status as umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the defendant's oath become required by consensus (ittifaq) in a claim of marriage?
A) Always, regardless of financial right.
B) Only when the claimant is a woman.
C) When the claim includes a financial right such as dower or maintenance.
D) Never, because marriage is a status claim.

Key Takeaway
In claims of personal status (marriage, raj'ah, fay', istilad, slavery, lineage) without any attached property, Abu Hanifa holds that no oath is required, unlike the Sahibayn who require an oath.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Oath in Pure Lineage Claims: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath-taking in pure lineage claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the administration of an oath in pure lineage claims, and apply the ruling (mufta bihi) in a practical scenario.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn treat refusal to swear as admission, so the oath is administered; Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees.

In claims of pure lineage (nasab mujarrad) or patronage (wala') without any accompanying property right, should a judge administer an oath to the defendant? Imam Abu Hanifa says no, while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), argue that the oath must be administered because refusal to swear (nukul) is effectively an admission. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its practical consequences in the Hanafi courtroom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claims Involved
Distinguish between pure lineage claims (e.g., 'This unknown person is my son' or 'You are my father') and lineage claims that also include property rights (inheritance, maintenance).
The latter type triggers a unanimous oath.
2
State the Dispute Core
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no oath is administered in pure lineage or wala' claims. The Sahibayn hold that an oath is administered.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's Reasoning
Understand why nukul (refusal) is considered iqrar (admission): the oath is an obligatory act for a truthful defendant, so refusal indicates falsehood.
The text explains that nukul has a semblance of payment (badhl) but is ultimately admission.
4
Apply the Limitations of Nukul
Note that nukul does not establish matters dropped by doubts (hudud, li'an) due to its semblance of payment. However, for lineage, it is effective because lineage can be established by admission in specific relations.
Admission in lineage is valid only for certain persons (e.g., parents, child, wife for men).
5
Determine the Practical Ruling
Later Hanafi practice follows the Sahibayn's view: the judge administers the oath, and refusal leads to judgment against the refuser.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

٥ و٦ . ورق ونسب : بأن ادَّعى على مجهول أنه قنهُ أو ابنه : وبالعكس بأن ادّعى مجهول الحال على رجل أنه مولاه، وأنكر المولى، أو ادَّعى مجهول الحال عليه أنه أبوه ، وهذا في دعوى نسب مجرد عن المال.
أما إذا ادعى مالاً بدعوى النَّسب بأن ادَّعى رجل على رجل أنه أخوه ، وقد مات الأب وترك مالاً في يد هذا، وطلب الميراث، أو ادَّعى على رجل أنه أخوه لأبيه ، وطلب من القاضي أن يفرض له النفقة، وأنكر المدعى عليه ذلك، فالقاضي يحلفه اتفاقاً ، صرح به العلامة الحموي وغيره.
وقال الإثقاني: يثبت الاستحلافُ عند أبي يوسف ومحمد له في النسب المجرَّدِ بدون دعوى حق آخر، ولكن يشترط أن يثبت النسب بإقرار المقرّ : أي يكون النسب بحيث يثبت بالإقرار، أما إذا كان بحيث لا يثبت النسب بإقرار المقر، فلا يجري الاستحلافُ في النسب المجرد.
وإنما يُسْتَخْلَفُ عندهما ; لأنَّ النُّكول إقرار ; لأنَّ الحلف واجب عليه على تقدير صدقه في إنكاره ، فإذا امتنعَ عُلِمَ أَنَّه غيرُ صادق في الإنكار، إذ لو كان صادقاً لأقدم على أداء الواجب، وهو الحلف، وإذا كان النكول إقراراً والإقرار يجري في هذه الأمور، فيحلف حتَّى إذا نَكَلَ مرَّة يُقْضَى بالنكول.
وعندهما أيضاً : بيانه : إن إقرار الرَّجل يصح بخمسة : بالوالدين والولد والزوجة والمولى ; لأنه إقرار بما لزمه، وليس فيه تحميل النسب على الغير، ولا يصح إقراره بما سواهم، ويصح إقرار المرأة بأربعة : بالوالدين والزوج والمولى، ولا يصح بالولد، ومن سوى هؤلاء ; لأنَّ فيه تحميل النسب على الغير إلا إذا صدقها الزوج في إقرارها بالولد أو تشهد لولادة الولد قابلة. صرَّحَ به الطحطاوي)، وغيره. ٧ - وولاء ; سواء كان ولاء العتاقة أو ولاء الموالاة بأن ادعى رجل على رجل معروف أنه مولاه، أو ادّعى المعروف ذلك وأنكر الآخر، فلا يحلف عند الإمام في هذه الأمور، وعندهما يحلف [ 1 ] قوله : لأنَّ النُّكول ... الخ ; تفصيلُه : إنَّ فائدة الحلف ظهور الحق بالنكول ، والنكولُ إقرار ; لأنَّ اليمين واجب ، فتركه دليل على أنه باذل أو مقر، ولا يمكن أن يجعل باذلاً ; لأنه يجوز ممن لا يجوز منه البذل كالمكاتب والعبد المأذون له في التجارة، وكذا يجوز في الدين، ولا يجوز بذله.
ويجب على القاضي أن يقضي بالنكول ويصح إيجابه في الذمَّةِ ابتداء، ولو كان بذلاً لما صح، ولا وجب، وكذا يجب القضاءُ به فيما دونَ النَّفْسِ فتعين أن يكون مقراً ، والإقرار يجري في هذه الأشياء لكنَّه إقرارٌ فيه شبهة البذل، فلا يثبت به ما يسقط بالشبهات كالحدودِ واللعان.
ألا ترى أنها لا تثبتُ بالشهادة على الشهادة ولا بكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي، ولا بشهادةِ النِّساء مع الرِّجالِ لما فيها من الشبهات، وهذا لأنَّ نكوله يدلُّ على أنه كاذب في الإنكار، ولولا ذلك لما تكل ; لأنَّ اليمين الصادقة فيها ثواب ذكرِ الله له على وجهِ التعظيم وصيانة مالِهِ وعرضه بدفعَ تُهمةِ الكذب عن نفسه، والعاقل يميل إلى مثل هذه ، واليمين الكاذبة فيها هلاك النفس.
5 and 6. Slavery and lineage: as when one claims against an unknown person that he is his slave or his son; and conversely, when a person of unknown status claims against a man that he is his master, and the master denies, or when a person of unknown status claims against him that he is his father. This is in a claim of lineage separate from property. As for when one claims property through a claim of lineage — such as a man claiming against another that he is his brother, and the father died leaving property in the hands of this one, and he claims inheritance; or he claims against a man that he is his paternal brother and asks the judge to award him maintenance, and the defendant denies — in such a case, the judge administers an oath to him by agreement. This was explicitly stated by al-Hamawi and others. Al-Ithqani said: The administering of an oath is established according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad for him in pure lineage without any other right, but with the condition that the lineage be such that it can be established by the admission of the person admitting: that is, the lineage must be of a type that is established by admission. However, if the lineage is not established by the admission of the person admitting, then the administering of an oath does not apply in pure lineage. And he is only administered an oath according to them because refusal (nukul) is admission. Because the oath is obligatory upon him on the assumption of his truthfulness in his denial. So if he refrains, it is known that he is not truthful in his denial, since if he were truthful he would have proceeded to perform the obligatory act, which is the oath. And when refusal is admission, and admission is valid in these matters, so he is made to swear, so that if he refuses once, judgment is passed on the basis of his refusal. And according to them also, its explanation: The admission of a man is valid regarding five: parents, child, wife, and master — because it is an admission of what is incumbent upon him, and there is no imposition of lineage upon others in it. His admission is not valid regarding others besides them. The admission of a woman is valid regarding four: parents, husband, and master — it is not valid regarding a child, nor anyone else besides these, because in that there is imposition of lineage upon others, unless her husband confirms her admission regarding a child or a midwife testifies to the child's birth. This was stated by al-Tahtawi and others. 7. And patronage (wala'), whether it is patronage of emancipation or patronage of alliance, as when a man claims against a known man that he is his patron (mawla), or the known person claims that and the other denies. In these matters, according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) he is not made to swear, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is made to swear. [1] His statement: 'Because refusal (nukul)...' etc. Its detail: The benefit of the oath is the appearance of the truth through refusal, and refusal is admission. Because the oath is obligatory, so its abandonment is evidence that he is either a spender (badhil) or an admitter (muqir). It cannot be considered as spending (badhl) because spending is permissible from someone from whom spending is not permissible, such as a mukatab or a slave permitted to trade, and similarly spending is permissible in matters of debt, but its spending is not permissible. It is obligatory upon the judge to pass judgment on the basis of refusal, and it is valid for him to obligate it in the dhimmah initially. If it were spending, it would not be valid nor obligatory. Similarly, judgment must be passed on it in matters less than life. So it is determined that he is an admitter. And admission is valid in these matters, but it is an admission that has a semblance of spending, so it does not establish what is dropped by doubts, such as hudud and li'an. Do you not see that they are not established by testimony upon testimony, nor by a judge's letter to a judge, nor by the testimony of women with men, due to the doubts in them? And this is because his refusal indicates that he is lying in his denial. Were it not for that, he would not speak, because the truthful oath contains the reward of remembering Allah with glorification and the preservation of his property and honor by removing the accusation of lying from himself. And a rational person is inclined to such things, while the false oath contains the destruction of the soul.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Kitab al-Da'wa, deals with three related claims: slavery (raq), lineage (nasab), and patronage (wala'). It first defines claims of slavery and lineage in two directions: claiming someone is your slave or son, and conversely a person of unknown status claiming someone is his master or father. These are pure lineage claims without property. Then it distinguishes a scenario where property is attached to the lineage claim, e.g., claiming inheritance or maintenance as a brother. In such cases, the judge administers an oath to the defendant by consensus. The core legal dispute (intra-Hanafi) is over pure lineage claims: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no oath is administered; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the judge does administer an oath. The reasoning of the Sahibayn is that nukul (refusal to swear) is considered an admission (iqrar) because the oath is obligatory upon the defendant if he is truthful. Therefore, if he refuses, it indicates he is not truthful, and this refusal is treated as an admission of the claim. This admission is valid in lineage matters, subject to certain conditions. The passage then details the rules of valid iqrar in lineage: a man's admission is valid regarding five persons (parents, child, wife, and master) because it only affects himself; a woman's admission is valid regarding four (parents, husband, master) but not regarding a child unless confirmed by the husband or a midwife. Finally, the same dispute applies to claims of wala' (patronage of emancipation or alliance): Imam does not administer an oath, while the Sahibayn do. A lengthy explanation follows, arguing that nukul cannot be treated as a voluntary payment (badhl) but rather as an admission, because payment is permissible from those who cannot pay, and it would not be obligatory. Hence, nukul is admission, but it has a semblance of payment, so it does not establish matters that are dropped by doubts (shubahat), like hudud and li'an. The passage strengthens this by noting that even testimony upon testimony or a judge's letter are not accepted in such cases due to doubts. Therefore, the Sahibayn's view is that the oath is administered in pure lineage and wala' claims, and refusal leads to judgment against the refuser.

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukul): The refusal of a defendant to take the oath after being directed by the judge; treated as an admission in certain cases.
الاستحلاف (al-istihlaf): The act of a judge administering an oath to a party in a dispute.
الولاء (al-wala'): Patronage relationship established by emancipation (wala' al-'itaqa) or by mutual agreement (wala' al-muwalat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is nukul (refusal to swear) considered an admission (iqrar) in a pure lineage claim?
A) Because the judge has the authority to force an admission.
B) Because the oath is an obligatory act for a truthful defendant, so refusal indicates falsehood.
C) Because the claimant has already proven the lineage with witnesses.
D) Because the defendant is afraid of committing perjury.

Key Takeaway
In pure lineage claims, the Sahibayn view (mufta bihi) allows the judge to administer an oath, treating refusal as admission, while Imam Abu Hanifa does not administer an oath.
